The weight_reg is also large.\n\nLet me compute the current VGPR usage and design the interleaved approach.\n\nThe key insight: `KD=3, KH=5, KW=5`. Current code reads `input_reg[3][5][3][2]` = 45 BF16 values per thread (stored as 45 float = ~45 VGPRs) before any MAC work. Weight reg adds `3*5*5 = 75 float`. The issue is that the wait is too conservative and serializes the ds_read + fmac pipeline.\n\nBetter approach: batch multiple ds_read calls before the wait, but still interleave in smaller batches than the original 45-read-all. In ROCm/HIP, a 1D array of BF16 is packed into 16-bit elements in one VGPR per stride. A 4D array might be allocated differently...\n\nThe key optimization should be reducing the *live range* of the weight_reg or the input_reg. So all 45 entries stay live during the reads (45 VGPRs) AND during all the fmacs (45 VGPRs still live). Plus weight_reg live through all fmacs. That's 45+75=120 minimum.\n\nBut wait, `IO_DTYPE` is 2 bytes. `IO_DTYPE[2]` is 4 bytes = the size of a dword. The compiler would allocate the 4D array as 3*5*3*2 = 90 16-bit elements, but might pack them as 45 32-bit VGPRs. So 45 VGPRs for input. Plus weight_reg = 75 float VGPRs. Plus sums, indices = ~5 VGPRs. Total ~125. The 155 VGPR actual count suggests inefficiencies in register allocation.\n\nMy 44-VGPR version uses `uint32_t reg[KWR]` (3 VGPRs) inside the (d,h) loop, which gets reused for each (d,h) pair. The weight_reg is still there but the compiler can be smarter about weight — since weight_reg is compile-time indexed by unrolled loops, the compiler may weight-load from kernel pointer on each access rather than keeping all 75 live.\n\nLet me try a different approach: what if I keep the original structure exactly but change `IO_DTYPE input_reg[KD][KH][KWR][KW_PACK]` to `uint32_t input_reg[KD][KH][KWR]`? That's just a type change that might help the compiler allocate better.\n\nI already tried that — 63 VGPRs. Still more than 44 but less than 155.
